Free Talk

A Small Statistic on the Native Places of the Martyrs of Huanghuagang 177

—Si Xuan

Today, nineteen years ago, is the anniversary of the martyrdom of our seventy-two martyrs in Guangzhou. The tragedy of their death can be immortalized in the history of the Republic of China. Since our Party unified the country, the names of the martyrs have become more prominent. Confucius said that it is to achieve benevolence, and Mencius said that it is to take righteousness. That is what it means. Among the martyrs, those from Guangdong are the most numerous, followed by Fujian. The two provinces of Guangdong and Fujian were the earliest to trade with Europe and the United States, and the most overseas Chinese reside there, and the oppression of imperialism is also the most severe. From this, we can know the vigorous spirit of the people of the two provinces, and it is no accident that the revolutionary base is named. The statistics of the native places of the martyrs are listed below.

Guangdong: Forty-one people

Fujian: Nineteen people

Guangxi: Six people

Sichuan: Three people

Anhui: Three people

In terms of counties, Huaxian, Guangdong, has reached seventeen people. Huaxian is the hometown of Hong Xiuquan, the leader of the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom. Perhaps the revolutionary spirit of the martyrs was influenced by Hong?

Eloquent Words of Huanghua 178

— Yan Qian

Collected Last Words of the Martyrs

A year passes easily. It is again the solemn and tragic Huanghua Festival. Therefore, I have collected the last words of the martyrs as "Eloquent Words of Huanghua" to commemorate them and to invigorate the national spirit. Dear readers of "Free Talk", have you ever considered that our freedom was not easily obtained? Then please read this article aloud as a tribute.

My revolution is based solely on what my heart believes in. If the heart believes, then act. This is true of Xu Xilin and Wen Shengcai. There is no such thing as an agreement or non-agreement. Everyone in the country is like this. Even Zhang Mingqi, Li Zhun, and you all are just blinded by profit and willingly act as slaves to the Manchus. If you were in my situation, could you guarantee that you would not be revolutionaries? I am performing my duty to save my compatriots. As for success or failure, that is up to Heaven. Who can avoid death? Why be stingy with it? (Confession of Martyr Pang Lie) The country is in turmoil, and the people are suffering. We should act with the hearts of sages and the deeds of heroes. (Words of Martyr Liu Yuandong) The purpose of the uprising is to awaken the compatriots from their dreams. What is meant by inciting rebellion? Sacrificing oneself to achieve benevolence is the teaching of the ancient sages. You are like rats! How can you know the great righteousness? Now that I have been captured, you are lost and will die! (Martyr Chen Gengxin said sternly to the Qing officials) A true man sacrifices his life for the country, it is his duty. Is it that I cannot achieve wealth and status? It's just that I am not like you, who recognize the thief as your father and know no shame. (Martyr Li Deshan cursed the executioner before execution) Do you think this act is a disgrace to warriors? The failure of the matter is Heaven's will. However, it can awaken our compatriots to continue the cause. You are blinded by profit and your blood has grown cold. How can you understand this? (Martyr Chen Kejun scolded the Qing officials) I have nothing to say to the Manchu slaves. (Martyr Cheng Liang was severely tortured by Li Zhun and cursed loudly like this. He then did not answer a single word.)

Returning from Attending the Opening of the Nanjing Grand Theater 179

— Sun Xin Fu

The Nanjing Grand Theater on Edward Road in this city opened on the 25th of this month. I was honored to receive a ticket to the theater from Mr. Yang Minshi, and was able to witness the grand occasion of the day. After returning, I will describe the scenes I saw in the theater in a jumbled manner.

The Architecture is Elegant and Refined - The exterior of the theater is built entirely of multi-colored artificial stone. The center is interspersed with beautiful and eye-catching bricks. The front faces north. Upon entering, there are silver-white, elegant sculptures that appear before our eyes. On both sides are the lower seats of the hall. In the middle is a stone staircase. Ascending the steps, to the north is the recreational corridor, and to the south are the upper seats. The seats above and below are very comfortable, and the facilities for adjusting the temperature are also very perfect. On the east side of the upper hall and the main hall, there are also very large rest rooms. The electric lights in the theater are of the indirect lighting type, which are bright without being dazzling. In short, the architecture of the theater can be called magnificent and elegant. Being in it is like being in a Roman palace.

Distinguished Guests Arrive - The theater was scheduled to open at 9:00 PM. However, by 8:30 PM, there were no empty seats upstairs and downstairs. For example, the Mayor of Shanghai Special Municipality Zhang Qun and the Songhu Garrison Commander Xiong Shihui both came with their families. When the band played the Party song, they stood up solemnly. Their lips moved slightly, probably humming the Party song in a low voice. A Little Sister Opens the Show - The opening performance featured a pair of innocent and lovely young girls under the age of ten. They were dressed in light red Western-style clothes and adorned with red satin flowers in their short hair. They were petite and exquisite, making people love them at first sight. It is said that this pair of little sisters are Miss Xu Miaoyu and Xu Miaosong, both daughters of the famous doctor Xu Yimin, and Mr. Xu is a director of the theater.

Humorous Songs - The film shown on the opening day was titled "Broadway", a latest full song and dance dialogue sound film produced by Universal Company of America. The scenery is magnificent. The plot is bizarre. The singers are like clouds, making people intoxicated. And there are many songs, most of which are melodious and moving. Among them, the song "Does the Chicken Lay the Egg or Does the Egg Lay the Chicken" is particularly humorous. The general idea is that eggs are laid by chickens, and chickens come from eggs. But is there first a chicken egg, and then a chicken, or first a chicken, and then an egg? Even college graduates cannot solve this problem. When the male lead sings this song, he wears a bachelor's cap and holds a stick, which is very humorous. This humorous song is set to a humorous tune, and then added with a humorous performance, which makes the audience even more unable to hold back their laughter.

The Old Fellow Townsman is Still Very Enthusiastic 180

— Plum Blossom Hermit

The old fellow townsman, Sun Juxian, is already ninety-one years old, but his spirit is still very robust. Last year, he performed a play to raise funds for the Yizhi Hall, and unexpectedly won great praise. This year, the Tianjin Red Swastika Society is experiencing financial difficulties, so it also used the old trick of the Yizhi Hall, asking the old fellow townsman to help greatly. It is scheduled to perform plays to raise funds on the 27th and 28th of this month. Although this old man is old, his enthusiasm is still not diminished. He readily agreed to the society's request, and volunteered to perform important good plays to attract attention. The first day will have two performances, one during the day called "Washing Silk" and one at night called "Fish Intestine Sword". The second day will be the full play "Four Jinshi". It is also heard that the ticket prices are very low, with downstairs seats costing one dollar and twenty cents per ticket, and boxes costing six dollars per room. (Recently, various small newspapers in this city have spread the rumor that old Sun has already come to Shanghai to perform on the Shanghai stage. However, inquiries from friends in Tianjin say that this is definitely not true. It is attached here to clarify the truth.)

A Record of a Strange Monk from Goryeo 181

— Qiu Shui

There is a famous monk in Goryeo named Shui Jinan (transliteration), who is currently fifty-six years old. He is energetic and has the appearance of a young man. He is an enlightened monk. According to what he told people, he has not eaten millet for several years. He only eats three pine nuts a day to live. He is confident that he can live to be over three hundred years old. Three years ago, Shui went to Japan and told the people in the Tokyo Noble Club that there is no other way to longevity than to calm the mind and reduce desires. Since I became enlightened, my living expenses have gradually decreased. Now I can live without spending a penny. What is the value of three pine nuts and a cup of clear water that I eat every morning and evening? During his speech, he took out pine nuts from his bag, which were the same as those we usually see in the mountains. A bag of pine nuts can last him three months of life. At this time when rice is as expensive as pearls and firewood as cinnamon, Shui is indeed a lucky child.

Twenty years ago, Shui was still working in the diplomatic office of the Korean-Japanese government. Then he served as a police patrolman in two major cities. Before long, he suddenly encountered a high monk, who passed on to him a Buddhist secret book. He became enlightened and resigned in 1917 to live his immortal life in the deep mountains and valleys. Shui was originally a devout Buddhist who studied Buddhism and had a lot of insights. According to what he told people, his longevity method was obtained from this secret book, and he worked hard to obtain it. After the founder of Buddhism, there were many who obtained his way and lived long, becoming immortals. The average lifespan could reach three hundred years. However, it was difficult to practice and was lost over time, so that today there are many who die young and have not heard of anyone who has lived to be over two generations. Shui has been practicing hard in the mountains for thirteen years. He has nothing to do on weekdays. He only enjoys sculpting Buddha statues. In the past thirteen years, it is said that he has made more than one thousand six hundred statues. Most of them are recorded in Buddhist books, but have not been seen by people. Shui's merits are also great. Recently, it was heard that his relatives and friends, as well as those in Japan who believe in him, are about to raise funds to build a temple for him in the mountain where he lives to enshrine the statues he has sculpted. The Japanese are inherently devout Buddhists, so this matter is probably within expectations. It is also heard that Shui will exert his remaining strength to search for the gods recorded in Buddhist scriptures who have been buried and are not prominent, and sculpt statues for them to enshrine, to spend his remaining years. He is confident that he still has over two hundred years of life, and does not need to ask Confucius to lend him a few more years to engage in his work. Record this to see what happens later.

Red Carpet

Miscellany of Travels in America from the Zhuiyu Studio 182

— Lai

After arriving in New York, I sent a letter, which should have arrived. On the 14th, Minister Wu invited the troupe to Washington to perform, specifically to introduce Wanhua to the political authorities and dignitaries from all walks of life. Unfortunately, President Hoover was away from Beijing on a trip and did not attend the grand event. After returning to Beijing, he heard about it and deeply regretted it. He immediately requested the Chinese Embassy to send someone to New York to discuss with Wanhua and perform again. If a solution is determined, it is bound to happen. The program for this performance was arranged by Mr. Zhang Pengchun (Zi Zhongshu, younger brother of Mr. Zhang Boling). Mr. Zhang has a deep understanding of drama and is particularly able to understand the psychology of the audience. His program and schedule are as follows:

Before the Curtain - Music (2 minutes) Explanation (5 minutes)

Fenhe Bay - Each scene after entering the kiln (27 minutes) Short break including curtain calls 4 minutes

Before the Curtain - Music 1 minute Explanation 3 minutes

Green Stone Mountain (rearranged) 9 minutes Short break including curtain calls 4 minutes

Before the Curtain - Music 1 minute Explanation 3 minutes

Stealing the Box and Dancing with the Sword 5 minutes Curtain call 1 minute Break 15 minutes

Before the Curtain - Music 3 minutes Explanation 5 minutes

Stabbing the Tiger 31 minutes Curtain call 1 minute

Total 120 minutes

The performance starts promptly at 9:00 PM and ends at 11:00 PM. Mr. Pengchun is in charge of the curtain. The punctuality is rarely seen in American theaters, and is especially commendable in Chinese theater. The explanation on stage is given by Ms. Yang from Guangdong. Her language is precise and extremely pleasant to listen to. The audience listens without any sign of fatigue. The performances focus on expression. After many rehearsals directed by Mr. Zhang, who also serves as the stage supervisor, the direction is smooth and his enthusiasm is admirable. The 16th was the day before the public performance. On that evening, famous New York playwrights, directors, and reporters were invited to the theater to watch the performance. This was the most critical moment. Praise or criticism would follow. Its nature was similar to undergoing a trial. However, after a song ended, not a single person did not express satisfaction. The next day, theater reviews were published in various newspapers, all of which praised the performance. The audience has been incredibly crowded for days. Whenever Wanhua finishes performing a scene, the applause from the audience is incessant. The curtain calls even reach six or seven times. For Chinese drama, which is completely different from Western interests, to be performed in America and be admired by the masses, it shows that art has no boundaries and has true value.

Plans After the Conclusion of the Honeybee Painting Exhibition 183

— Swallow

The Honeybee Society Painting Exhibition, initiated by famous painters Zheng Wuchang, Xu Zhao, Qian Shoutie, Sun Xueni, He Tianjian, etc., lasted for a week. Visitors were very crowded. The collaborative fan paintings during the remaining events were especially welcomed by customers. Hu Peiran and Liu Dingsan even bought more than ten fan paintings, showing great interest. The book exhibition in the last three days was also very enthusiastic. Some people who already had painted fans asked for collaborative calligraphy. Ren Jinshu, Zheng Wuchang, Qian Shoutie, Xie Gongzhan, Ye Weishen, Sun Xueni, etc. collaborated on regular, cursive, clerical, and seal scripts, which was most rare. According to statistics, the results of the ten days were very good. At the closing ceremony, Qian Shoutie proposed that the remaining paintings and fan paintings be donated to charitable organizations to benefit the public. The proposal was approved by everyone. Zheng Wuchang proposed to set up an art lecture series, inviting famous artists to teach the advanced members of the society, and to set up a Honeybee Club as a place for members to collaborate and gather. The charter was drafted that day and will be announced later. It is heard that more than a hundred people have joined the society. Among them, Hu Ruosi is only fifteen years old, while Xu Chunxi is already seventy-seven years old. One old and one young, painting fan paintings together at the meeting, is truly an elegant event. By the time the meeting was dismissed and the curtain closed, the remaining lamps had already leaked. I am writing this down to record the event's grandeur.

Warmth in My Heart (158) 184

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Ten: Blazing Flames Soar, and the Courtesan Pays Homage to Filial Piety. The Red Carpet is Laid, and Famous Actors are Met Immediately.

However, Fengyun still felt a little unconvinced in her heart, often making cold remarks and adding a kind of cold laughter. She was originally a frustrated politician in this room, and they regarded her as a reactionary element in general. Today, everyone crowded around to see this photo, and seeing Zuo Shichen acting as if he was doing something important to check their fingers, Fengyun first curled her lips and let out a cold laugh from her nose, saying, "Second Master, then let me take a bath and then come and see it. Didn't the ancients have to bathe in fragrant water before receiving the emperor's edict so that they could open it and read it?" Zuo Shichen was so stumped by her that he couldn't open his mouth, saying, "No, no. Looking at photos often leaves two fingerprints, which is very ugly. I also had a photo the other day that everyone was looking at, and it left several fingerprints. I used an eraser to try to erase them, but they wouldn't come off. Moreover, some people even talk to the photos, and the saliva splashes on the photos, which is also very annoying." At that time, Fengyun had already pouted and walked away, not wanting to look. Hanyun and others were more honest, saying, "My fingers are very clean, and I definitely won't leave any fingerprints." After a while, they discussed what kind of frame to use and where to hang it. It wasn't until eleven o'clock that Ruiyun finally came back. Zuo Shichen thought to himself at that time, "Ruiyun must be very happy to see this photo, because she has already asked several times if the photo is ready and how come it hasn't been printed after a week." She also said, "I know that everyone else's photos are taken very well, but only mine is taken the worst. If it's not taken well, I'd rather not have it." But Shichen teased her and said, "It's no use if you don't want it. Everyone else's photos are taken very well, so they will naturally want to take them. You can't cut yourself out of the twelve people." Saying this made her even more worried. She said, "Then what should I do? Thank you. Can you help me think of a way?" Zuo Shichen said, "Don't worry. Your photo isn't taken badly. I've already seen it on the glass plate. Not only is it not bad, but it's also taken very naturally and freely." She said that she hadn't seen it herself and couldn't believe it. She had to see it with her own eyes before she could feel relieved. But now that it's been developed, it's indeed not taken badly. She was relieved to see this photo. Since it was taken very well, she was naturally very happy to see it. Zuo Shichen felt that seeing Ruiyun's happiness was like his own happiness, because Ruiyun came back every day after finishing her performance at around eleven o'clock. Although she was inevitably a little tired, she was very happy. Sometimes she was even very happy, because she had a kind of lively and innocent childlike spirit, quite like the "Aijiao" that the Japanese talk about. She sometimes had a face full of Aijiao, not restrained at all. And it wasn't anything frivolous. In that kind of intentional or unintentional question, there seemed to be a kind of pure and genuine character, which made Zuo Shichen think of her running barefoot in the desolate garden in Nanjing.

British and Japanese Cotton Industry Agreement 193

When the British and Japanese relations are discussed, the answers to the questions will be found. Zhabei: Yesterday, the source was still small, and the river channel was also not smooth. The production price of coarse rice from the inside roads remained difficult to lower. Route goods were slightly better by 0.02 to 0.03 yuan, but only several thousand bags were offered. 2,000 tons were opened for distant deliveries, and the price was similar to the previous market.

Annan Indica Rice Will Arrive in Shanghai Soon 197

Annan coarser-grained indica rice, similar to river-bottom indica rice, is welcomed by Shanghai merchants who need to sell it as river-bottom rice. Unfortunately, the production is small and arrivals are scarce, making it difficult to maintain a presence in the market for a long time. Yesterday, 1,000 bags of recent goods were sold, with delivery expected in about a week, priced at 16.20 yuan. Those for delivery in three or four days were priced at 16.30 yuan, it is said.

Flour Market's Speculation is Hot 198

Yesterday's flour market saw different perspectives after the morning opening. Although the quoted price for foreign wheat saw a slight decrease again, the speculative craze of internal and external longs did not pay attention at all. Their only goal was because the largest factory was selling very few goods. Although small and medium-sized factories were selling a considerable amount, it seemed that outsiders occupied half of the April and May volume. The longs raised the price at will, which is so-called holding for higher prices. In terms of actual sales, Tianjin's Hehua brand is not selling, and Shanghai's Shen flour sales will inevitably decrease from now on (the current Tianjin inventory of both local and foreign flour totals 2.2 to 2.3 million bags). The market price of foreign wheat, excluding the premium, is similar to that of local wheat. If factories have the capacity to maintain the price of goods, they should seize foreign wheat as a future means of relief. Otherwise, the longs' momentum will be difficult to calm down for a while. As a result, this month was 0.025 yuan better than the previous day, April was 0.075 yuan, May was 0.01 yuan better, June was 0.025 yuan better, July was slightly 0.025 yuan worse, and August was 0.025 yuan better, it is said.

Wheat Futures Still in Progress 199

Yesterday's wheat futures market, after the opening in the morning and afternoon, this month's contracts had already been settled and there was no market. The other months remained firm due to outside interest, so the opening price rose again. According to recent conditions, April's contracts are still mostly held by factories among the longs. If high-priced goods are scarce in the future, they will inevitably be squeezed again. As for the distant months, inland merchants, in light of the soaring rice prices, are still strongly interested in buying, so the future trend is still more likely to rise than fall. As a result, April was 0.01 yuan better than the previous day, June and July were each 0.01 yuan better, and August was 0.02 yuan better. Spot wheat was generally stable, but the high-priced goods on the market were all being delivered at the exchange. The goods that were being traded were all of medium to lower quality, so the price felt cheaper. The opening price was 5.11 taels for Jiangsu and Suzhou wheat, 5 taels for Jiangxi wheat, 4.96 taels, 4.92 taels, 5.08 taels for Mingguang wheat, 4.92 taels for Anqing wheat, 4.82 taels, 4.6 taels, 4.72 taels for Shashi wheat, 4.57 taels for Hankou wheat, 4.53 taels, 4.33 taels, for a total of 5,000 bags, which was handled by Shen Dahua Feng, it is said.

Yesterday, the standard Lianyuan beans fell sharply due to a telegram from Dalian reporting a decline. The spot opening price entered the 7 yuan level, so selling interest in Shanghai turned strong. The recent price fell back to 5.29 taels, a drop of more than 0.005 taels. The guild's spot goods were still relatively flat in the early morning, but also turned weak in the afternoon. Inland merchants' demand was very small, so transactions were few. Only three carriages of Pingge grade were transacted, with the price opening at 5.4 taels. Both arrivals and sales of Yangtze River beans were weak, and the market was also poor.

Silk and Tea: Silk Market Benefits from Cocoon Shortage and High Costs 202

Dry Cocoon Base Requires Net Pull of Over 1,000 Taels

Dry cocoon inventory is thin and cannot be replenished. Last year, various silk factories reduced work and stopped machines in order to regulate production. This spring, European and American silk merchants, due to the surge in gold prices and higher prices for Japanese silk, abandoned Japan and turned to China. Shanghai silk sales turned smooth. However, cocoon inventory became increasingly scarce. The current market price for spring dry cocoons in Wuxi is over 170 taels per dan. When 600 catties are reeled, the net cocoon cost per silk bag requires a pull of 1,020 to 1,030 taels. The silk cost is still high, so the silk market is increasingly firm and selling well. Yesterday morning, there were continued telegrams from Europe turning to Shanghai, and Chinese merchants' attitudes became firmer. Yesterday, Lan Lebi and others entered 60 bales of Shanghai white factory warp, Xinfu entered 20 bales of Shandong yellow factory warp, and Dachang entered 20 bales of gray warp. Prices were still profitable.

Youth Garden

The Tutoring System at Great China University 207

— Zhi Jing

The authorities at our school, Great China University, considering the difficulty students face in choosing careers and the complexity of social life, wanted to provide appropriate guidance before students leave the school. This would enable them to adapt appropriately to social and professional life after graduation. Also, as Vice-President Ou said, another reason was: "Nowadays, schools place too much emphasis on formalities. Students attend classes to obtain certificates, and teachers teach to receive salaries. The relationship between teachers and students is limited to a specific time. Once that time is over, they go their separate ways. Teachers don't know their students, and the responsibility of guidance is lost. Students don't understand their teachers, and the idea of learning from them disappears. If they don't communicate with each other, how can there be any instruction? But it doesn't stop there. In recent years, schools have been in turmoil, and student movements have been rampant. There have even been instances of students beating teachers, and student killings of principals are not unheard of. The friendship between teachers and students has completely vanished. The drawbacks of this are countless." Therefore, they considered advocating a tutoring system.

The tutoring system at Great China University was implemented in the first semester of last year. At that time, based on a resolution by the Academic Affairs Council, twenty-one current professors were appointed as tutors. They were under the Academic Affairs Office and initially only applied to fourth-year students in the liberal arts, science, commerce departments, and second-year students in the advanced normal program. At that time, there were more than one hundred and seventy students being tutored. The Academic Affairs Office distributed students to various tutors based on their department, major, hometown, and other factors. Each tutor was responsible for guiding about ten students. This was the first trial implementation of the tutoring system at Great China University. The procedure at the time was that the Dean of Academic Affairs first convened a general discussion, explaining the history of tutoring systems in European and American universities, the purpose of implementation at our school, and points to be noted. Afterwards, they proceeded in groups. The methods of each group were slightly different, including holding tea parties, dinner parties, and even outings and excursions, to achieve the purpose of meeting and talking. As for the content of the discussions, it was truly complex and covered everything: personal cultivation, family and marriage, current affairs, career choices after graduation, and anything else that was relevant. Although there were considerable achievements, it was a pity that the implementation time was too short, only about a week before the approaching graduation exams. In the following semester, because of the initial experiment, the results were still fairly satisfactory, so it was decided to continue with many improvements, roughly as follows:

1. Expand the scope of the tutoring system from fourth-year students in each department to third-year students in each department. The number of tutors was also increased proportionally.

2. Because the tutoring system seemed to have the nature of extracurricular work, the University Affairs Council decided to transfer it to the Committee on Group Education.

3. After discussion by the Committee on Group Education, in order to suit the psychology of the students, it was decided to allow students to choose their own tutors. As a result, the school was enthusiastic.

The above three points are roughly the improvements made in the previous semester, and because of the longer duration, the results were better.

The semester has just started, and the school authorities, in order to meet the needs of the students, are continuing to work tirelessly. They have already announced the list of students who will be under the tutoring system this semester and have resolved on three measures, which are recorded below:

1. Students in the original groups, except for those who have graduated, will still be guided by their original tutors. Students promoted this semester will be allowed to choose their own tutors and then be assigned.

2. Freshmen will be guided separately by the deans of each college, the heads of each department, and the heads of each major.

3. Measures:

A. Notify the deans of each college, the heads of each department, and the heads of each major by letter, and attach a list of freshmen, asking them to meet and talk with the freshmen at any time. B. Announce this measure to all freshmen.

Therefore, in the conversations of our classmates, we can often hear them telling each other that the discussion with a certain tutor was interesting, that a certain tutor's treatment was generous, and even talking about how delicious the food was at the dinner party. Naturally, we will also find many interesting stories in the process, and I will report on them continuously when I have the opportunity.
